Scheduler skips the rest of these plugins as soon as one returns success.\n\tBind PluginSet `json:\"bind,omitempty\"`\n\n\t// PostBind is a list of plugins that should be invoked after a pod is successfully bound.\n\tPostBind PluginSet `json:\"postBind,omitempty\"`\n\n\t// MultiPoint is a simplified config section to enable plugins for all valid extension points.\n\t// Plugins enabled through MultiPoint will automatically register for every individual extension\n\t// point the plugin has implemented. Disabling a plugin through MultiPoint disables that behavior.\n\t// The same is true for disabling \"*\" through MultiPoint (no default plugins will be automatically registered).\n\t// Plugins can still be disabled through their individual extension points.\n\t//\n\t// In terms of precedence, plugin config follows this basic hierarchy\n\t//   1. Specific extension points\n\t//   2. Explicitly configured MultiPoint plugins\n\t//   3. The set of default plugins, as MultiPoint plugins\n\t// This implies that a higher precedence plugin will run first and overwrite any settings within MultiPoint.\n\t// Explicitly user-configured plugins also take a higher precedence over default plugins.\n\t// Within this hierarchy, an Enabled setting takes precedence over Disabled. For example, if a plugin is\n\t// set in both `multiPoint.Enabled` and `multiPoint.Disabled`, the plugin will be enabled. Similarly,\n\t// including `multiPoint.Disabled = '*'` and `multiPoint.Enabled = pluginA` will still register that specific\n\t// plugin through MultiPoint. \\t\\t// We treat it as: the plugin is not interested in any event, and hence pod failed by that plugin\\n386: \\t\\t// cannot be moved by any regular cluster event.\\n387: \\t\\t// So, we can just fn,\\n409: \\t\\t\\t})\\n410: \\t\\t}\\n411: \\t\\tif registerNodeAdded && !registerNodeTaintUpdated {\\n412: \\t\\t\\t// Temporally fix for the issue https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/109437\\n413: \\t\\t\\t// NodeAdded QueueingHint isn't always called because of preCheck.\\n414: \\t\\t\\t// It's definitely not something expected for plugin developers,\\n415: \\t\\t\\t// and registering UpdateNodeTaint event is the only mitigation for now.\\n416: \\t\\t\\t//\\n417: \\t\\t\\t// So, here registers UpdateNodeTaint event for plugins that has NodeAdded event, but don't have UpdateNodeTaint event.\\n418: \\t\\t\\t// It has a bad impact for the requeuing efficiency though, a lot better than some Pods being stuch in the\\n419: \\t\\t\\t// unschedulable pod pool.\\n420: \\t\\t\\t// This behavior will be removed when we remove the preCheck feature.\\n421: \\t\\t\\t// See: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/110175\\n422: \\t\\t\\tqueueingHintMap[framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.Node, ActionType: framework.UpdateNodeTaint}] =\\n423: It starts scheduling and blocked until the context is done.\\n435: func (sched *Scheduler) Run(ctx context.Context) {\\n436: \\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\\n437: \\tsched.SchedulingQueue.Run(logger)\\n438: \\n439: \\t// We need to start scheduleOne loop in a dedicated goroutine,\\n440: \\t// because scheduleOne function hangs on getting the next item\\n441: \\t// from the SchedulingQueue.\\n442: \\t// If there are no new pods to schedule, it will be hanging there\\n443: \\t// and if done in this goroutine it will be blocking closing\\n444: \\t// }\n371: \n372: func buildQueueingHintMap(es []framework.EnqueueExtensions) internalqueue.QueueingHintMap {\n373: \tqueueingHintMap := make(internalqueue.QueueingHintMap)\n374: \tfor _, e := range es {\n375: \t\tevents := e.EventsToRegister()\n376: \n377: \t\t// This will happen when plugin registers with empty events, it's usually the case a pod\n378: \t\t// will become reschedulable only for self-update, e.g. schedulingGates plugin, the pod\n379: \t\t// will enter into the activeQ via priorityQueue.Update().\n380: \t\tif len(events) == 0 {\n381: \t\t\tcontinue\n382: \t\t}\n383: \n384: \t\t// Note: Rarely, a plugin implements EnqueueExtensions but returns nil.\n385: \t\t// We treat it as: the plugin is not interested in any event, and hence pod failed by that plugin\n386: \t\t// cannot be moved by any regular cluster event.\n387: \t\t// So, we can just ignore such EventsToRegister here.\n388: \n389: \t\tregisterNodeAdded := false\n390: \t\tregisterNodeTaintUpdated := false\n391: \t\tfor _, event := range events {\n392: \t\t\tfn := event.QueueingHintFn\n393: \t\t\tif fn == nil || !utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.SchedulerQueueingHints) {\n394: \t\t\t\tfn = defaultQueueingHintFn\n395: \t\t\t}\n396: \n397: \t\t\tif event.Event.Resource == framework.Node {\n398: \t\t\t\tif event.Event.ActionType&framework.Add != 0 {\n399: \t\t\t\t\tregisterNodeAdded = true\n400: \t\t\t\t}\n401: \t\t\t\tif event.Event.ActionType&framework.UpdateNodeTaint != 0 {\n402: \t\t\t\t\tregisterNodeTaintUpdated = true\n403: \t\t\t\t}\n404: \t\t\t}\n405: \n406: \t\t\tqueueingHintMap[event.Event] = append(queueingHintMap[event.Event], &internalqueue.QueueingHintFunction{\n407: \t\t\t\tPluginName:     e.Name(),\n408: \t\t\t\tQueueingHintFn: fn,\n409: \t\t\t})\n410: \t\t}\n411: \t\tif registerNodeAdded && !registerNodeTaintUpdated {\n412: \t\t\t// Temporally fix for the issue https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/109437\n413: \t\t\t// NodeAdded QueueingHint isn't always called because of preCheck.\n414: \t\t\t// It's definitely not something expected for plugin developers,\n415: \t\t\t// and registering UpdateNodeTaint event is the only mitigation for now.\n416: \t\t\t//\n417: \t\t\t// So, here registers UpdateNodeTaint event for plugins that has NodeAdded event, but don't have UpdateNodeTaint event.\n418: \t\t\t// It has a bad impact for the requeuing efficiency though, a lot better than some Pods being stuch in the\n419: \t\t\t// unschedulable pod pool.\n420: \t\t\t// This behavior will be removed when we remove the preCheck feature.\n421: \t\t\t// See: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/110175\n422: \t\t\tqueueingHintMap[framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.Node, ActionType: framework.UpdateNodeTaint}] =\n423: \t\t\t\tappend(queueingHintMap[framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.Node, ActionType: framework.UpdateNodeTaint}],\n424: \t\t\t\t\t&internalqueue.QueueingHintFunction{\n425: \t\t\t\t\t\tPluginName:     e.Name(),\n426: \t\t\t\t\t\tQueueingHintFn: defaultQueueingHintFn,\n427: \t\t\t\t\t},\n428: \t\t\t\t)\n429: \t\t}\n430: \t}\n431: \treturn queueingHintMap\n432: }\n433: \n434: // Run begins watching and scheduling. It starts scheduling and blocked until the context is done.\n435: func (sched *Scheduler) Run(ctx context.Context) {\n436: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n437: \tsched.SchedulingQueue.Run(logger)\n438: \n439: \t// We need to start scheduleOne loop in a dedicated goroutine,\n440: \t// because scheduleOne function hangs on getting the next item\n441: \t// from the SchedulingQueue.\n442: \t// If there are no new pods to schedule, it will be hanging there\n443: \t// and if done in this goroutine it will be blocking closing\n444: \t// SchedulingQueue, in effect causing a deadlock on shutdown.\n445: \tgo wait.UntilWithContext(ctx, sched.ScheduleOne, 0)\n446: \n447: \t<-ctx.Done()\n448: \tsched.SchedulingQueue.Close()\n449: \n450: \t// If the plugins satisfy the io.Closer interface, they are closed.\n451: \terr := sched.Profiles.Close()\n452: \tif err != nil {\n453: \t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Failed to close plugins\")\n454: \t}\n455: }\n456: \n457: \treturn informerFactory\n463: }\n464: \n465: func buildExtenders(logger klog.Logger, extenders []schedulerapi.Extender, profiles []schedulerapi.KubeSchedulerProfile) ([]framework.Extender, error) {\n466: \tvar fExtenders []framework.Extender\n467: \tif len(extenders) == 0 {\n468: \t\treturn nil, nil\n469: \t}\n470: \n471: \tvar ignoredExtendedResources []string\n472: \tvar ignorableExtenders defaultQueueingHintFn = func(_ klog.Logger, _ *v1.Pod, _, _ interface{}) (framework.QueueingHint, error) {\n\treturn framework.Queue, nil\n}\n\nfunc buildQueueingHintMap(es []framework.EnqueueExtensions) internalqueue.QueueingHintMap {\n\tqueueingHintMap := make(internalqueue.QueueingHintMap)\n\tfor _, e := range es {\n\t\tevents := e.EventsToRegister()\n\n\t\t// This will happen when plugin registers with empty events, it's usually the case a pod\n\t\t// will become reschedulable only for self-update, e.g. schedulingGates plugin, the pod\n\t\t// will enter into the activeQ via priorityQueue.Update().\n\t\tif len(events) == 0 {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// Note: Rarely, a plugin implements EnqueueExtensions but returns nil.\n\t\t// We treat it as: the plugin is not interested in any event, and hence pod failed by that plugin\n\t\t// cannot be moved by any regular cluster event.\n\t\t// So, we can just ignore such EventsToRegister here.\n\n\t\tregisterNodeAdded := false\n\t\tregisterNodeTaintUpdated := false\n\t\tfor _, event := range events {\n\t\t\tfn := event.QueueingHintFn\n\t\t\tif fn == nil || !utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.SchedulerQueueingHints) {\n\t\t\t\tfn = defaultQueueingHintFn\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\tif event.Event.Resource == framework.Node {\n\t\t\t\tif event.Event.ActionType&framework.Add != 0 {\n\t\t\t\t\tregisterNodeAdded = true\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\tif event.Event.ActionType&framework.UpdateNodeTaint != 0 {\n\t\t\t\t\tregisterNodeTaintUpdated = true\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\tqueueingHintMap[event.Event] = append(queueingHintMap[event.Event], &internalqueue.QueueingHintFunction{\n\t\t\t\tPluginName:     e.Name(),\n\t\t\t\tQueueingHintFn: fn,\n\t\t\t})\n\t\t}\n\t\tif registerNodeAdded && !registerNodeTaintUpdated {\n\t\t\t// Temporally fix for the issue https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/109437\n\t\t\t// NodeAdded QueueingHint isn't always called because of preCheck.\n\t\t\t// It's definitely not something expected for plugin developers,\n\t\t\t// and registering UpdateNodeTaint event is the only mitigation for now.\n\t\t\t//\n\t\t\t// So, here registers UpdateNodeTaint event for plugins that has NodeAdded event, but don't have UpdateNodeTaint event.\n\t\t\t// It has a bad impact for the requeuing efficiency though, a lot better than some Pods being stuch in the\n\t\t\t// unschedulable pod pool.\n\t\t\t// This behavior will be removed when we remove the preCheck feature.\n\t\t\t// See: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/110175\n\t\t\tqueueingHintMap[framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.Node, ActionType: framework.UpdateNodeTaint}] =\n\t\t\t\tappend(queueingHintMap[framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.Node, ActionType: framework.UpdateNodeTaint}],\n\t\t\t\t\t&internalqueue.QueueingHintFunction{\n\t\t\t\t\t\tPluginName:     e.Name(),\n\t\t\t\t\t\tQueueingHintFn: defaultQueueingHintFn,\n\t\t\t\t\t},\n\t\t\t\t)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn queueingHintMap\n}\n\n// Run begins watching and scheduling. It starts scheduling and blocked until the context is done.\nfunc (sched *Scheduler) Run(ctx context.Context) {\n\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n\tsched.SchedulingQueue.Run(logger)\n\n\t// We need to start scheduleOne loop in a dedicated goroutine,\n\t// because scheduleOne function hangs on getting the next item\n\t// from the SchedulingQueue.\n\t// If there are no new pods to schedule, it will be hanging there\n\t// and if done in this goroutine it will be blocking closing\n\t// SchedulingQueue, in effect causing a deadlock on shutdown.\n\tgo wait.UntilWithContext(ctx, sched.ScheduleOne, 0)\n\n\t<-ctx.Done()\n\tsched.SchedulingQueue.Close()\n\n\t// If the plugins satisfy the io.Closer interface, they are closed.\n\terr := sched.Profiles.Close()\n\tif err != nil fn,\n\t\t\t})\n\t\t}\n\t\tif registerNodeAdded && !registerNodeTaintUpdated {\n\t\t\t// Temporally fix for the issue https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/109437\n\t\t\t// NodeAdded It starts scheduling and blocked until the context is done.\nfunc (sched *Scheduler) Run(ctx context.Context) {\n\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n\tsched.SchedulingQueue.Run(logger)\n\n\t// We need to start scheduleOne loop in a dedicated goroutine,\n\t// because scheduleOne function hangs on getting the next item\n\t// from the SchedulingQueue.\n\t// If there are no new pods to schedule, it will be hanging there\n\t// and if done in this goroutine it will be blocking closing\n\t// SchedulingQueue, in effect causing a deadlock on shutdown.\n\tgo wait.UntilWithContext(ctx, sched.ScheduleOne, 0)\n\n\t<-ctx.Done()\n\tsched.SchedulingQueue.Close()\n\n\t// If the plugins satisfy the io.Closer interface, they are closed.\n\terr := sched.Profiles.Close()\n\tif err != nil
